deprecate_posargs(deprecation_warning, remappable_names, /):\n101:     \"\"\"\n102:     Function/method decorator to deprecate some or all positional arguments.\n103: \n104:     The decorated function will map any positional arguments after the ``*`` to\n105:     the corresponding keyword arguments and issue a deprecation warning.\n106: \n107:     The decorator takes two arguments: a RemovedInDjangoXXWarning warning\n108:     category and a list of parameter names that have been changed from\n109:     positional-or-keyword to keyword-only, in their original positional order.\n110: \n111:     Works on both functions and methods. To apply to a class constructor,\n112:     decorate its __init__() method. To apply to a staticmethod or classmethod,\n113:     use @deprecate_posargs after @staticmethod or @classmethod.\n114: \n115:     Example: to deprecate passing option1 or option2 as posargs, change::\n116: \n117:         def some_func(request, option1, option2=True):\n118:             ...\n119: \n120:     to::\n121: \n122:         @deprecate_posargs(RemovedInDjangoXXWarning, [\"option1\", \"option2\"])\n123:         def some_func(request, *, option1, option2=True):\n124:             ...\n125: \n126:     After the deprecation period, remove the decorator (but keep the ``*``)::\n127: \n128:         def some_func(request, *, option1, option2=True):\n129:             ...\n130: \n131:     Caution: during the deprecation period, do not add any new *positional*\n132:     parameters or change the remaining ones. For example, this attempt to add a\n133:     new param would break code using the deprecated posargs::\n134: \n135:         @deprecate_posargs(RemovedInDjangoXXWarning, [\"option1\", \"option2\"])\n136:         def some_func(request, wrong_new_param=None, *, option1, option2=True):\n137:             # Broken: existing code may pass a value intended as option1 in the\n138:             # wrong_new_param position.\n139:             ...\n140: \n141:     However, it's acceptable to add new *keyword-only* parameters and to\n142:     re-order the existing ones, so long as the list passed to\n143:     @deprecate_posargs is kept in the original posargs order. This change will\n144:     work without breaking existing code::\n145: \n146:         @deprecate_posargs(RemovedInDjangoXXWarning, [\"option1\", \"option2\"])\n147:         def some_func(request, *, new_param=None, option2=True, option1):\n148:             ...\n149: \n150:     The @deprecate_posargs decorator adds a small amount of overhead. In most\n151:     cases it won't be significant, but use with care in performance-critical\n152:     code paths.\n153:     \"\"\"\n154: \n155:     def decorator(func):\n156:         if isinstance(func, type):\n157:             raise TypeError(\n158:                 \"@deprecate_posargs cannot be applied to a class. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_0163duvhTzTRYnjgdX3dZ4b3","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_0126iVNFXvGZcvcSwC91uirm","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/django/middleware/ratelimit.py","content":"\"\"\"\nRate Limiting Middleware.\n\nThis module provides middleware for implementing per-IP request rate limiting\nusing Django's cache framework.\n\"\"\"\n\nfrom django.conf import settings\nfrom django.core.cache import cache\nfrom django.http import HttpResponseTooManyRequests\nfrom django.utils.deprecation import MiddlewareMixin\n\n\nclass RateLimitMiddleware(MiddlewareMixin):\n    \"\"\"\n    Middleware for rate limiting requests based on client IP address.\n\n    Uses Django's cache framework to track request counts per IP.\n    Returns HttpResponseTooManyRequests (429) when the rate limit is exceeded.\n\n    Configuration via settings:\n    - RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS: Number of requests allowed per window (default: 100)\n    - RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW: Time window in seconds (default: 3600)\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def process_request(self, request):\n        \"\"\"\n        Check if the request exceeds the rate limit for the client's IP.\n        \"\"\"\n        # Get rate limit settings with defaults\n        limit_requests = getattr(settings, \"RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS\", 100)\n        limit_window = getattr(settings, \"RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW\", 3600)\n\n        # Get client IP address\n        client_ip = request.META.get(\"REMOTE_ADDR\", \"unknown\")\n\n        # Create cache key for this IP\n        cache_key = f\"ratelimit:{client_ip}\"\n\n        # Get current request count for this IP\n        request_count = cache.get(cache_key, 0)\n\n        # Check if limit exceeded\n        if request_count >= limit_requests:\n            return HttpResponseTooManyRequests()\n\n        # Increment request count\n        cache.set(cache_key, request_count + 1, limit_window)\n\n        # Allow the request to proceed\n        return None\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":2,"cache_creation_input_tokens":524,"cache_read_input_tokens":58420,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":524},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"1caa3b41-f391-4259-b83c-368275d8e343","uuid":"8a7217e3-f64f-44a7-be25-28dca087d92b"}
